166 class StepOptimization(UpdateStep , object):
167
'''An extension of the UpdateStep algorithm which covers step-based
updaters in general.
==PAGE:155==
A.2 Code
147
168
A step-based update algorithm is understood to be one where a step
update , modified by some step length ,
169
is added to the current state to make the new updated state. It covers
e.g. gradient methods.
170
171
Internal Variables:
172
model, bound -- Linked objects. see the "UpdateStep" docstring.
173
stepgenerator -- A generator object which supplies a sequence of
step-lengths.
174
Default is a constant step length of 1.0.
175
steplength -- the step length supplied by the "stepgenerator".
176
direction -- The step direction used in the update step. Computed
in the "refresh" method.
177
'''
178
def __init__(self, model, bound, parameter , logupdate = False):
179
'''Constructs a StepOptimization object.
180
Extends the UpdateStep constructor with
a default step generator
181
and initializes internal variables.
182
'''
183
super(StepOptimization , self).__init__(model, bound, parameter)
184
self.stepgenerator = annealing_scheme()
185
self.step_type = 'adadelta'
186
self.logupdate = logupdate
187
self.steplength = 0.0
188
self.parameter = parameter
189
self.index = Ellipsis
190
self.direction = 0.0
191
self.accumulate_direction = 0.0
192
self.accumulate_step = 0.0
193
self.shift = 0.78 #0.35
194
self.weight = 0.04#0.1
195
self.learning_rate = 1e-3
196
197
def refresh(self, state):
198
'''Computes a new step length and new step direction.'''
199
super(StepOptimization , self).refresh(state)
200
self.finddirection()
201
self.accumulate_direction = ((1.0-self.weight)*self.
accumulate_direction +
202
self.weight*(self.direction)**2)
203
self.get_steplength()
204
205
def step(self):
206
'''Takes a step of size "self.steplength" in the direction
specified by "self.direction".'''
207
if self.index is None:
208
self.index = Ellipsis
209
current_parameter = self.model.param[self.parameter][self.index]
210
211
step = self.steplength*self.direction
212
self.accumulate_step = (1.0-self.weight)*self.accumulate_step +
self.weight*(step)**2
==PAGE:156==
148
A Grid Searches
213
#switch between ordinary and logarithmic update
214
if self.logupdate:
215
update = np.exp(np.log(current_parameter)+step)
216
else:
217
update = current_parameter + step
218
219
return self.model.set[self.parameter](update, index = self.index)
220
221
def get_steplength(self):
222
'''retrieve step length for next gradient step.
223
Switches on 'self.step_type'.
224
Options include:
225
identity - step length of 1.0
226
constant - arbitrary constant step length
227
generator - step lengths generated by generator object
228
adagrad - adaptive scheme by Duchi
229
adadelta - adaptive scheme by Zeiler
230
adadelta_annealed - adadelta combined with generator
231
'''
232
if self.step_type == 'adadelta' or self.step_type == '
adadelta_annealed':
233
self.steplength = np.sqrt(self.accumulate_step+self.shift)/np.
sqrt(self.accumulate_direction+self.shift)
234
if self.step_type == 'adadelta_annealed':
235
self.steplength *= self.stepgenerator.next()
236
elif self.step_type == 'adagrad':
237
self.steplength = self.learning_rate/np.sqrt(self.
accumulate_direction+self.shift)
238
elif self.step_type == 'identity':
239
self.steplength = 1.0
240
elif self.step_type == 'constant':
241
self.steplnegth = self.learning_rate
242
elif self.step_type == 'generator':
243
self.steplength = self.stepgenerator.next()
244
else:
245
raise ValueError(self.step_type + ' is not a valid step
generation scheme!')
246
247
def finddirection(self):
248
pass
249
250
def setgenerator(self, generator):
251
'''Set a new step generator'''
252
self.stepgenerator = generator

.parameter ,

index = self.index, sample = sample))

288 class NaturalConjugate(StepOptimization , object):

'''Experimental natural conjugate ascent algorithm'''

fisher_dict = {'beta': fisher_beta , 'mult': fisher_mult}

def __init__(self, model, bound, parameter , distribution_type):
293

294
self.natgrad_new = None

def finddirection(self):
304
'''compute conjugate search direction'''
305

306

self.natgrad_new , self.model.distribution[self.parameter])

beta = self.conjugate_correction()
==PAGE:158==
150
A Grid Searches
308
self.direction = self.natgrad_new +beta*self.direction
309
310
def conjugate_correction(self):
311
'''compute the conjugate gradient weight'''
312
self.inner_new = self.natgrad_new.ravel().dot(self.grad_new.ravel
())
313
if self.inner_previous is None:
314
return 0.0
315
inner_mixed = self.natgrad_previous.ravel().dot(self.grad_new.
ravel())
316
upper = (self.inner_new -inner_mixed)
317
lower = self.inner_previous
318
if upper < self.tolerance or lower < self.tolerance:
319
return 0.0
320
beta = upper/lower
321
return np.nan_to_num(max(beta, 0.0))
322

327
self.natgrad_previous = self.natgrad_new
328
self.grad_previous = self.grad_new

330 class LineSearch:
331
'''LineSearch objects faciliate line search algorithms.
332
LineSearch ensures that all steps are correct and do not result
333
in additional work.
334
It incorporates Wolfe search and backtracking as well as Wolfe
conditions.
335
'''
336
def __init__(self, scheduler):
337
self.scheduler = scheduler
338
self.change = {}
339
self.at_step = 0.0
340

341
self.max_step = 1.5 #maximum step allowed by line searches
342
self.backtrack_factor = 0.9
343
self.constants = [1e-4, 0.7] #Wolfe condition constants
344
self.original_value = 0.0
345
self.original_directional = 0.0
346
self.previous_value = None
347
self.previous_directional = None
348
self.value = None
349
self.directional = None
350
self.iteration = 0
351
self.maxit = 20 #maximum number of allowed iterations
352
353
def get_directional_derivative(self):
354
'''get directional derivative at current step'''
355
gradient = self.scheduler.bound.complete_gradient()
356
increase = 0.0
==PAGE:159==
A.2 Code
151
357
for key in gradient.iterkeys():
358
direction = self.scheduler.updater[key].direction
359
increase += direction.ravel().dot(gradient[key].ravel())
360
self.previous_directional = self.directional
361
self.directional = increase
362
return self.directional
363
364
def get_value(self):
365
'''get objective value at current step'''
366
self.previous_value = self.value
367
self.value = self.scheduler.bound.calculatebound()
368
return self.value
369
370
def goto(self, step):
371
'''update algorithm as if a step of size 'step' was taken from
point of origin'''
372
take_step = step - self.at_step
373
self.at_step = step
374
for parameter in self.scheduler.model.parameters:
375
self.scheduler.updater[parameter].steplength = take_step
376
self.change[parameter] = self.scheduler.update(parameter)
377
378
def reset(self):
379
'''prepare for new line search'''
380
self.iteration = 0
381
self.at_step = 0.0
382
self.change = {}
383
self.previous_directional = None
384
self.previous_value = None
385

386

387
self.directional = self.original_directional
388
self.value = self.original_value
389

def armijo(self):
392
'''Evaluate Armijo/sufficient increase condition , return boolean
'''
393
sufficient_increase = self.constants[0]*self.at_step*self.
original_directional
394
if sufficient_increase < 1e-16:
395
return True
396
return self.value - self.original_value >= sufficient_increase
397
398
def wolfe_curvature(self):
399
'''Evaluate Wolfe curvature condition , return boolean'''
400
return abs(self.directional) <= self.constants[1]*abs(self.
original_directional)
401
402
def backtrack(self):
403
'''Run backtracking line search. Start at start_step and pull back
incrementally
==PAGE:160==
152
A Grid Searches
404
by a factor of 'self.backtrack_factor' until sufficient increase
condition holds

'''

408
while self.iteration < self.maxit:
409
self.goto(step)
410
self.get_value()
411
if self.armijo():
412
return self.change
413
else:
414
step *= self.backtrack_factor
415
self.iteration += 1
416
return self.change
417

def wolfesearch(self):
419
'''Run Wolfe search algorithm to find step observing both Wolfe
conditions.'''

428
self.zoom(before, current)

431

432

433
self.zoom(before, current)
434
return self.change
435
before = current
436
current = self.bisect(current , self.max_step)
437
self.iteration += 1
438
return self.change

def bruteforce(self, steps):
471
'''Calculate all steps along current search direction and return
objective values.'''
472
values = np.zeros_like(steps)
473
for index, step in enumerate(steps):
474
self.goto(step)
475
values[index] = self.get_value()
476

def interpolate(self, start, end):
479
'''Propose new step size in interval'''
480
try:
481
return self.cubic(start, end)
482
except TypeError:
483
return self.bisect(start, end) #self.base_quadratic(high)
484
485
def cubic(self, start, end):
486
'''Apply Davidons cubic interpolation in interval (start,end) to
propose step'''
487
if self.previous_directional < 0:
488
return self.bisect(start, end)
489
beta = end - start
490
#print "interpolation derivative:", self.previous_directional
491
e = (3.0/beta)*(self.previous_value -self.value)+self.
previous_directional+self.directional
492
h = np.sqrt(e**2-self.previous_directional*self.directional)
493
num = self.previous_directional + e - h
494
denom = self.directional+self.previous_directional + 2*e
495
medstep = beta*(num/denom)
496
step = start+beta*(num/denom)
497
if np.isnan(step) or step < start or step > end:
498
return self.bisect(start,end)
499
return step

def bisect(self, low, high):
502
'''Propose center of interval as new step size'''
503
return (low + high)/2.0

def flipsearchdirection(self):
506
'''Flip direction of search'''
507

508
temp_value = self.value
509
self.directional = self.previous_directional
510
self.value = self.previous_value
511
self.previous_directional = temp_directional
512
self.previous_value = temp_value

APPENDIX B
Time Plan
B.1
Problem Statement
• What is the state-of-the-art in variational inference (VI)?
• How does stochastic variational inference (SVI) allow us to tackle large-scale prob-
lems?
• How are Bayesian nonparametric relational models structured?
• How does SVI compare to existing inference methods?
B.2
Learning Goals
• can identify and reﬂect on technical scientiﬁc issues and understand the
interaction between the various components that make up an issue
We explore relational problems, how they can be modelled in a statistical sense,
and how these models can be used to draw sensible conclusions.
• can, on the basis of a clear academic proﬁle, apply elements of current
research at international level to develop ideas and solve problems
We study and apply novel research on methods such as stochastic variational in-
ference from 2013-2014 and state-of-the-art Bayesian nonparametric models.
• masters technical scientiﬁc methodologies, theories and tools, and has
the capacity take a holistic view of and delimit a complex, open issue,
see it in a broader academic and societal perspective and, on this basis,
propose a variety of possible actions
We investigate the relational problem theoretically and empirically, building on
existing knowledge and results drawn from implementations of the algorithms in
question.
• can, via analysis and modelling, develop relevant models, systems and
processes for solving technological problems
We consider the general relational modeling problem and adapt existing algorithms
to new applications.
• is familiar with and can seek out leading international research within
his/her specialist area.
The project is deeply rooted in state-of-the-art academic research.

156

Figure B.1: Time allocation.
Essentials covers the study of the papers and texts which act as the foundation of the
thesis.
Research includes extensions and examinations of the subjects covered in the essential
papers.
Modelling this task covers adapting theory to models, and will be carried out inter-
mittently to adapt the research to the project.
Implementation covers implementing the models in legible and functional code.
Writing time dedicated to producing the thesis paper. The ﬁnal months will be spent
on writing almost exclusively, but preliminary chapters will also be written in the
earlier months to document accomplished research.
B.4
Evaluation
I evaluate that the learning goals have been met, but it is unfortunate that I did not
get to pursue stochastic variational inference for a more suitable model. A lot of time
was spent trying to ﬁnd a stochastic approximation method for the IRM, and while we
have detailed a valid stochastic approximation approach it is hardly as advantageous as
stochastic variational inference.
We set out to make a thesis with a strong focus on theory, and I believe it succeeds
in this aspect as it manages to cover most of the topics from a proper theoretical angle
instead of solely relying on empirical evidence. We do end up running the algorithms on
real-world data, but that was never really the goal of this thesis and is more of a proof
==PAGE:165==
B.4 Evaluation
157
of concept. Better results could deﬁnitely have been achieved by spending more time
on a single learning problem, but we chose to approach the topics from a more general
angle.
More time was spent on programming than initially expected, but it is diﬃcult to
talk about algorithms without being able to demonstrate them, and my understanding
of the models was strengthened by this hands-on element.
